  51. First off...it doesn't hurt at all, even when applying considerable pressure. No pain and no bleeding, just some redness and slight sensitivity that lasts for about an hour after use. This surprised me because of the needles length. I thought it would be painful. So glad it is not. Anyway, this is the skin rolling routine I use for my oily skin. First I wash with a gentle foaming cleanser and I do two or three passes. Then I soak a cotton pad with medical grade (higher then 70%) alcohol and wipe my face not only to prep for the roller, but also to ensure that there is no trace of cleanser left. I also dip the roller head in the alcohol as well and then start rolling as per the directions that came with the unit. I roll until my face is very red and then I apply a sheet mask, usually My Beauty Diary's Bulgarian White Rose, or something similar that is gentle and non-irritating. I leave the mask on for longer than the recommended 15 minutes...usually 45 minutes to an hour. Then I remove it and just let my skin sit for another 10 minutes and then I apply an eye cream to the eye contours and a light moisturizer to the rest of my face and that's it. I do this two to three times a week, always before bedtime. That way, my skin has a chance to really relax. In the morning my skin is very smooth and silky with no trace of redness. Then I just splash my face with cool water, apply a toner and moisturizer, and go about my day. The results are obvious...my entire face is more toned and the contours are more defined, especially my cheeks. Plus the skin itself has a finer texture and looks very smooth and silky..almost like a child's (and I'm really &#34;over the hill&#34;, so that's saying a LOT). I really believe that this roller combined with a healthy lifestyle can work wonders on anyone's skin...you only have to give it a chance. :-)

  491. As far as the product is concerned, it's sturdy, well put together, etc. That's not why it receives a low rating. I would not recommend it because it's a concept that is highly dangerous. Allowing skin to regenerate itself by producing collagen as a result of 'damaging', or pricking in this case, the skin, mostly face, is the latest hot procedure within the esthetician/med spa community. Yes, I've had it done, but the point is they are trained practitioners using a sterile safe device AND have to numb your skin prior to use. Nerve endings are more exposed through thin skin or skin that doesn't have a fat layer like forehead. Putting this product in the hands of the layman is inviting trouble and possible permanent damage. Is this product cheaper....by leaps and bounds. Does it come with proper instruction.....yes, very well explained. Should anyone not trained use it.....absolutely not.

  553. I'm quite disappointed in the quality of this roller. While it is marketed as a micro needle roller, the sharp bits are actually micro \\"knives\\" that are stamped out of a disc of metal rather than individual cylindrical needles mounted into the head. This creates cuts in the skin (which might actually harm the skin as it cuts into collagen fibers laterally) rather than piercing the skin vertically to create a channel. Because the construction of this unit is hard to ascertain without taking a magnifying glass to it, I used this for a year and was confused by why my results have not been as good with this roller as with my previous (***different brand***) roller, which used true needles. In searching for answers, I came across an online derma roller review page where they include this 540 \\"needle\\" roller and saw the magnified photo showing the head of stamped \\"knives\\". I then took a magnifying glass to my own roller -- indeed, the \\"needles\\" on this unit are identical to this photo of micro \\"knives\\". I feel misled by the marketing by this roller, as these micro-blades may actually be harmful to use, and because the aforementioned web site also suggests that this stamped-knife design is less expensive to manufacture than the true needle design. The clinical results in the dermatology literature are from using a product with true needles, and in retrospect I would have rather purchased a unit with fewer true \\"needles\\" for the same cost. I regret falling into the \\"more-needles = better\\" mentality, and will be looking for an alternative product! I wish I had discovered the construction of the \\"needles\\" on this unit before the end of the return period.   586. After doing quite a bit of reading and research I decided to get the 1.0mm roller for my face. Let me say it does not hurt at all! I began rolling very lightly and was able to increase pressure right away...but I did not put heavy pressure as this is contraindicated for any rolling. It actually felt good...sounds weird but true. Afterward my face was red like a light sunburn and that is normal. It was actually more uncomfortable after rolling than during as it felt like a sunburn, which again is normal. I used my all natural products following the procedure. The next day my face was still had a sunburn appearance until mid afternoon and I rolled the night before. My face felt tight and smooth. My main goal is to even out skin tone, erase darkly pigmented areas and produce collagen to fill in some forehead lines that are starting and lines vertical frown lines on the inner sides of my eyebrows.<br /><br />I am a RN and after much research here are my recommendations:<br />- Make sure and cleanse face thoroughly prior to rolling and clean face with alcohol on cotton fully two times...with fresh cotton swab on second time.<br />- Make sure hair is pulled back completely<br />- Soak your roller in at least 70% alcohol 15-30 min prior to procedure and afterwards<br />- Make sure to only use 100% natural products on your face afterwards! This is very important so read your labels thoroughly. Since the absorption of the product you use on your fact afterward is increased +1000x or more, you must use all natural even organic products. No chemicals. This was recommend on reputable research material over and over.<br />- DO NOT roll more than every 30 days. I know there are a lot of reviews where people are rolling several times a week, every two weeks, etc. But I have done the medical research on this and for collagen formation, if you roll more often than every 30 days the collagen production cycle will be interrupted and it will defeat the purpose. Yes, people do see increased &#34;fullness&#34; in their face and diminished lines when they roll more often, but this is not attributed to collagen being produced...but it is attributed to the tissue being in a constant state of inflammation. Read the cycle of collagen production at the cellular level and you will understand why rolling more often is contraindicated and will work against the formation of collagen and not for it. This process takes time...many months for your body to produce the amount of collagen to fill in lines and that is based off medical research.<br /><br />Because this process takes many months to see the true results and you will need to roll monthly up to 18 months or more to achieve maximum results (although visible results will be noticeable in 6 months) I can only give a four star rating now but will update later.
